## Section 001: Rust Backend Testing Fixtures
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title pairs testing with fixtures but the seed never states the file's central inversion, for HTTP backends the outside-in integration test is the primary instrument and unit tests are the specialists, reserved for domain constructors, validation, parsing edges, and small pure decisions
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the inversion exists because backend defects cluster in wiring, serialization, routing, and state setup, faults that live between units, so tests entering through the public HTTP interface catch what unit tests structurally cannot see
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reading the file as generic test advice misses that its harness, port, database, and mocking sections all serve the one inversion, they are the infrastructure bill the outside-in stance requires teams to pay
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference covers endpoint verification, harness structure, isolated infrastructure, mocking, helpers, and the test matrix, what to build is the playbook theme and how to deploy is the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the inversion, integration-first with unit tests as domain specialists, and present the remaining sections as its supporting machinery
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Testing Fixtures", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the file assigns each test kind a jurisdiction rather than a rank, the matrix maps six concerns to preferred test types, so the real doctrine is not integration tests are better but each defect class has one cheapest catcher, choose by concern

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the matrix converts suite review from taste into table lookup, a change touching a concern row without its assigned test class is a visible gap, so gating on the matrix is gating on a checkable artifact rather than on reviewer intuition
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: gating only on tests pass admits suites whose green status covers the wrong concerns, the matrix exists because passing is meaningless when endpoint behavior is certified by unit tests that never crossed the wire

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: engineers who have only read the sections assemble them wrong under deadline, a spawned app against a shared database, or a mock asserting nothing about the outbound shape, integration theater that the walkthrough's assertions would have caught

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed compile-centric indicator ignores suite feedback, nothing counts defects caught by integration tests versus escaped to production, flake rate as the isolation-debt signal, or matrix coverage per concern row across the suite
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each ratio measures one doctrine claim in operation, catch-versus-escape tests the integration-first bet, flake rate tests the isolation rules, and matrix coverage tests whether the concern-to-class assignments are actually being honored
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the ratios the integration-first stance stays a creed, and creeds lose to deadlines the first quarter someone proposes skipping the harness work because unit tests are faster to write
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: measuring this theme's suite disciplines, pipeline health belongs to the ops theme's loop and dispatch discipline to the entry theme's
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the three ratios with their collection points, defect retrospectives for catch-versus-escape, CI retry records for flake rate, and the suite manifest's matrix block for coverage

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed endpoint-count budgets fit request work, not suite work, whose real units are founding cost per service paid once for harness and isolation, marginal cost per test riding the standing infrastructure, and maintenance cost per infrastructure change when migrations or dependencies shift under the suite
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the three units scale on different axes, founding scales with service count, marginal cost scales with test count and dominates authoring economics, and maintenance scales with schema and dependency churn, so a single number cannot budget them together
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: budgeting suites at marginal cost alone is the classic error, the first integration test costs days because it carries the harness, and plans that price it like the fiftieth test conclude falsely that integration testing is too expensive to start
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: budgeting suite effort for services adopting this theme, application-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and rollout budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the model in three units, founding cost per service, marginal cost per test with the harness as its divisor, and maintenance cost per infrastructure shift
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the file's economics run on one ratio, founding cost divided across all future tests, every harness improvement is a price cut on every subsequent test, which is why the dependency-chain ordering front-loads exactly the work that compounds
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to budget the founding as a project, drive marginal cost down through harness quality, and slot maintenance into every schema or dependency change rather than deferring it
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the three units scale on different axes, founding scales with service count, marginal cost scales with test count and dominates authoring economics, and maintenance scales with schema and dependency churn, so a single number cannot budget them together
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; budgeting suites at marginal cost alone is the classic error, the first integration test costs days because it carries the harness, and plans that price it like the fiftieth test conclude falsely that integration testing is too expensive to start
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: budgeting suite effort for services adopting this theme, application-slice budgets belong to the playbook theme and rollout budgets to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: restate the model in three units, founding cost per service, marginal cost per test with the harness as its divisor, and maintenance cost per infrastructure shift
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the file's economics run on one ratio, founding cost divided across all future tests, every harness improvement is a price cut on every subsequent test, which is why the dependency-chain ordering front-loads exactly the work that compounds

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: targets averaged over time hide the binary ones, one live external call in the deterministic suite is one nondeterminism source taxing every build, not a tolerable percentage

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand where suite retry doctrine should, a failing test and a flaking test demand opposite responses, deterministic failures are signal to fix forward, while retry-until-green on a flake is evidence destruction, each retry teaches the team the suite lies
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the file's isolation rules exist precisely so failures are deterministic, when they are, rerunning changes nothing and fixing is the only move, and when they are not, the flake is an isolation-debt report whose correct handling is diagnosis, not dice-rolling
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: auto-retry policies that rerun failed tests until they pass convert the suite's honesty into noise, masked flakes accumulate as isolation debt while green builds certify less each week, the suite equivalent of rerunning a failed migration blindly
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: retry semantics for suite failures, application-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the two-regime rule, no automatic retries in the deterministic suite, and a diagnose-then-quarantine path for detected flakes with the quarantine list burning down visibly
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that one deliberate rerun is legitimate as an instrument, running a suspected flake twice distinguishes deterministic from intermittent, the regime forbids retry as acceptance while keeping it as diagnosis, the same action with opposite meanings depending on what consumes the result
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to fail the build on any deterministic-suite failure, route detected flakes to quarantine with an owner and a deadline, and cap the quarantine list as a standing gate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the file's isolation rules exist precisely so failures are deterministic, when they are, rerunning changes nothing and fixing is the only move, and when they are not, the flake is an isolation-debt report whose correct handling is diagnosis, not dice-rolling

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the two-regime rule, no automatic retries in the deterministic suite, and a diagnose-then-quarantine path for detected flakes with the quarantine list burning down visibly

### Question 06: Which gotchas and failure modes matter most?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: the highest-value warnings are backpressure applies to suite growth, a team whose quarantine list grows monthly should stop adding integration tests and repay isolation debt first, more tests on a flaking foundation multiply the noise, not the coverage
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: these warnings deserve priority because auto-retry policies that rerun failed tests until they pass convert the suite's honesty into noise, masked flakes accumulate as isolation debt while green builds certify less each week, the suite equivalent of rerunning a failed migration blindly
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: do not classify ordinary variation as failure when the pipeline distinguishes suites, a deliberately non-deterministic staging-contract suite may retry within stated bounds, the deterministic one may not
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: evaluate each warning inside this assumption set: retry semantics for suite failures, application-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: add observable warning signs plus the recovery path statistical flake detection that reruns everything and reports pass rates, informative at platform scale, it institutionalizes the retry-as-acceptance habit the regime exists to forbid
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 06 on gotchas and failure modes: explain the systemic effect that one deliberate rerun is legitimate as an instrument, running a suspected flake twice distinguishes deterministic from intermittent, the regime forbids retry as acceptance while keeping it as diagnosis, the same action with opposite meanings depending on what consumes the result
### Question 07: What do good, bad, and borderline examples look like?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the operational comparison is Good: a red build fixed forward because the failure reproduced identically twice. Bad: a merge on the third rerun's green. Borderline: rerunning once to classify a suspected flake, legitimate exactly when the result routes to quarantine rather than to merge
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the good case is credible because the pipeline distinguishes suites, a deliberately non-deterministic staging-contract suite may retry within stated bounds, the deterministic one may not
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: the borderline case must expose the limit that the quarantine-list cap that balances honesty against delivery pressure is team-calibrated
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: interpret all three examples within retry semantics for suite failures, application-level retry doctrine belongs to the security sibling's territory one layer down
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: revise the examples so each reveals a decision, consequence, and recovery while implementing this section-specific change: add the two-regime rule, no automatic retries in the deterministic suite, and a diagnose-then-quarantine path for detected flakes with the quarantine list burning down visibly
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 07 on good, bad, and borderline examples: use the comparison to surface this deeper lesson: one deliberate rerun is legitimate as an instrument, running a suspected flake twice distinguishes deterministic from intermittent, the regime forbids retry as acceptance while keeping it as diagnosis, the same action with opposite meanings depending on what consumes the result

- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: that deduction follows from the file's isolation rules exist precisely so failures are deterministic, when they are, rerunning changes nothing and fixing is the only move, and when they are not, the flake is an isolation-debt report whose correct handling is diagnosis, not dice-rolling

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: change the guidance by applying this concrete revision: add the two-regime rule, no automatic retries in the deterministic suite, and a diagnose-then-quarantine path for detected flakes with the quarantine list burning down visibly
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 10 on second-order deductions: the resulting operational insight is to change course when the default is unsafe or insufficient, using these bounded alternatives: statistical flake detection that reruns everything and reports pass rates, informative at platform scale, it institutionalizes the retry-as-acceptance habit the regime exists to forbid This changes how the section resolves which suite failures may rerun and what any rerun's result is allowed to mean.

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic counters replace the record set suite work needs, which tests ride the harness versus bypass it, which resources each test isolates versus shares, which external behaviors each mock simulates, and which matrix rows each substantial change claims to cover
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each record serves a distinct consumer, harness records serve the bypass probe, isolation records serve the flake investigator, mock inventories serve the rot probe, and mapping records serve the matrix gate, the four probes of the failure table each need their record stream
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: unrecorded mock behavior is the quiet loss, a mock's simulated responses live only in test code, so when the real API drifts nobody can list what the suite believes about it without reading every mock, the inventory is what makes rot detectable
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: what suite work must record, service runtime telemetry belongs to the ops theme's checklist
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the emission floor, harness usage visible per test, isolation semantics in the manifest, mock inventory per external system, and matrix mapping per substantial PR, kept in the artifacts the discipline already produces

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed request-latency ceilings measure the service, this theme's performance surfaces are suite wall time as the delivery tax every merge pays, per-test setup cost as the isolation price, and time-to-first-test on a new service as the founding friction
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the file's choices all spend suite performance to buy trust, real migrations, per-test provisioning, and spawned apps each cost seconds, so the doctrine's sustainability depends on those seconds staying bounded, an unmeasured suite quietly becomes the bottleneck its critics predicted
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: ignoring suite performance lets it decay until developers stop running tests locally, at which point defects surface in CI or later, the trust the infrastructure bought is refunded as latency
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: verifying suite performance, service latency belongs to the playbook theme's SLO clause and pipeline duration to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure the three surfaces with trend alarms, total wall time per suite run, setup-versus-assertion time split per test, and calendar time from service founding to first green integration test
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the setup-versus-assertion split is the diagnostic ratio, a suite whose runtime is mostly setup is paying isolation costs that parallelization or template databases can cut without touching a single assertion, the split says where optimization is safe
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to record the three measurements per release and investigate any surface whose trend breaks its historical band
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the file's choices all spend suite performance to buy trust, real migrations, per-test provisioning, and spawned apps each cost seconds, so the doctrine's sustainability depends on those seconds staying bounded, an unmeasured suite quietly becomes the bottleneck its critics predicted

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed document-scale bounds stand where suite scale seams should, the file's guidance assumes one service, one database, and a suite one team runs whole, and each assumption has a breaking point, multi-service integration exceeding the spawned-app harness, shared datastores breaking per-test provisioning, and suite duration forcing selective execution
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the harness spawns one application, so tests spanning services need contract tests or environment-level orchestration the file does not cover, and per-test database provisioning assumes a database the test owns, both assumptions named in the file's own mechanics
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: stretching the harness across seams produces the worst of both worlds, multi-service tests through one service's harness assert against half a system, and shared-store provisioning that pretends to isolate reproduces the undocumented-sharing anti-pattern at architecture scale
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: bounding this theme's suite doctrine, service architecture seams belong to the playbook theme and rollout seams to the ops theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to name the three seams with their triggers, a second service in one journey triggers contract-test strategy, a shared datastore triggers schema-level isolation design, and suite duration past local patience triggers tiered execution with honest tier labels
